## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The variables describe population size P over time t with target dP_dt, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics. Common relationships model per-capita growth as a function of density (P) and/or time-varying forcing (t), yielding ODEs for dP_dt.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Constant net growth (baseline drift): dP_dt = c0 (constant immigration/emigration or net births minus deaths independent of P)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth rate)
- Power-law per-capita growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (allometric or aggregation effects when growth scales nonlinearly with P)
- Linear density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth when c1 < 0)
- Logistic ODE (Verhulst form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) (carrying capacity via negative quadratic term)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P**c2) (flexible density dependence shape via exponent c2)
- Gompertz growth (continuous): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth declines logarithmically with density)
- Ricker-type continuous form: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (strong density dependence with exponential suppression at high P)
- Allee effect (weak/strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) (reduced growth at low density due to mate-finding/cooperation)
- Cubic Allee + carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (low-density inhibition plus high-density limitation)
- Harvesting/constant removal: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) - c2 (logistic growth with constant-yield harvest/harvesting effort)
- Seasonal forcing of growth or capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) - P) (periodic environment affecting growth/carrying capacity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth rate inference: if dP_dt / P is approximately constant, prefer dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent growth); if dP_dt / P decreases with P, include density dependence.
- Carrying capacity signature: dP_dt crosses zero at a positive P and becomes negative for larger P → include a factor like (c1 - P) or (c1 - P**c2).
- Allee signature: dP_dt negative at small positive P but positive at intermediate P → include (P - c1) (or higher-order factors) to create a low-density threshold.
- Asymmetric approach to equilibrium: rapid early growth but very slow approach near the upper bound can favor Gompertz form dP_dt ∝ P * log(c/P) over quadratic logistic.
- Overcompensatory density dependence: growth suppressed more sharply than quadratic at high P suggests an exponential term exp(-c*P) multiplying P (Ricker-like).
- External removal/stocking: persistent negative offset in dP_dt across P indicates additive terms (±c0) rather than purely multiplicative P terms.
- Seasonality/periodicity: oscillations in dP_dt at similar P values over time suggests adding sin(c*t + c) modulation to growth rate or carrying capacity.
- Multiple equilibria: evidence of three zero-crossings of dP_dt vs P (extinction threshold, stable intermediate/upper states) suggests cubic products P*(P-c1)*(c2-P).

Expand the polynomial part:
\[
0.953996983528\,P \;-\;\frac{0.953996983528}{96.9068829767}P^2 \;+\;0.953996983528\,P^{1/3}
\]
So GT is exactly a linear combination of three basis functions in \(P\) only:
\[
A\,P^{1/3} + B\,P^2 + C\,P
\]
with \(A=0.953996983528\), \(C=0.953996983528\), \(B=-0.953996983528/96.9068829767\), and **no \(t\)-dependence**, no constant offset, no other nonlinearities.

Below, each candidate matches GT iff we can (i) eliminate any \(t\)-dependent terms by setting their coefficients to 0, and (ii) make the remaining \(P\)-dependence exactly \(A P^{1/3}+B P^2 + C P\) (no extra terms like constants, logs, exp, sin, rational-in-\(P\), etc.).

---

### 1. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2t + P^{c3}c4 + c5 t^{c6} + c7 t\)
Set \(c2=c5=c7=0\) to remove \(t\). Need \(P^{c3}c4\) to be \(A P^{1/3}\): set \(c3=1/3,\; c4=A\). Then set \(c0=B,\; c1=C\). Works. **Match.**

### 2. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + \frac{c3 t}{(P+c4)^3} + c5 t (P+c6)^{c7}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence for all \(t\): set \(c3=0,\; c5=0\). Remaining is \(c0P^{1/3}+c1P^2+c2P\). Choose \(c0=A,c1=B,c2=C\). **Match.**

### 3. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + \frac{Pc3}{(c4 t + c5)} + c6 + \frac{c7}{(c4 t + c5)}\)
Terms with \((c4 t+c5)^{-1}\) depend on \(t\) unless their numerators are 0: set \(c3=0,c7=0\). Then there is still an additive constant \(c6\), but GT has no constant term, so set \(c6=0\). Remaining matches by \(c0=A,c1=B,c2=C\). **Match.**

### 4. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3\log(c4 t + 1) + \frac{c5 t}{(P+c6)^3}\)
Remove \(t\): need \(c3=0\) and \(c5=0\). Then match via \(c0=A,c1=B,c2=C\). **Match.**

### 5. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3 t^{c4} + \frac{c5 t}{(P+c6)^3}\)
Remove \(t\): set \(c3=0,c5=0\). Then match with \(c0=A,c1=B,c2=C\). **Match.**

### 6. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3 e^{Pc4} + c5\)
To match GT, must eliminate \(e^{Pc4}\) unless it can become a polynomial/ \(P^{1/3}\) term. Exponential cannot equal a combination of \(P^{1/3},P,P^2\) for all \(P\) unless coefficient is 0: set \(c3=0\). Also GT has no constant, so set \(c5=0\). Then match with \(c0=A,c1=B,c2=C\). **Match.**

### 7. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3 e^{Pc4}\)

### 8. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P^{c2}c3 + c4 e^{Pc5} + c6\log(Pc7+1)\)

### 9. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + \frac{c3 t}{(P+c4)^3} + c5\sin(c6 t+c7)\)

### 10. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P^{c2}c3 + c4 e^{Pc5}\)

### 11. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3 + c4\sin(c5+c6 t)\)

### 12. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3 e^{Pc4} + \frac{c5 t}{(P+c6)^3}\)

I need to determine which candidates are mathematically equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.9540*(1 - P/96.907)*P + 0.9540*P^(1/3)`

Expanding: `0.9540*P - 0.009845*P² + 0.9540*P^(1/3)`
